</div><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Chinese web services company</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1320445320">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For the medieval person, see <a href="/wiki/Family_of_Demetrius_II_of_Georgia" title="Family of Demetrius II of Georgia">Family of Demetrius II of Georgia</a>.</div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"BIDU" redirects here. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Bidu_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Bidu (disambiguation)">Bidu</a>.</div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Beidu_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Beidu (disambiguation)">Beidu (disambiguation)</a>, <a href="/wiki/BeiDou" title="BeiDou">BeiDou</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Badu_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Badu (disambiguation)">Badu (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

href="/wiki/Cantonese" title="Cantonese">Yue: Cantonese</a></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Yale_romanization_of_Cantonese" title="Yale romanization of Cantonese">Yale Romanization</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><span title="Yue Chinese-language romanization"><span style="font-style: normal" lang="yue-Latn">Baakdouh</span></span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Jyutping" title="Jyutping">Jyutping</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><span title="Yue Chinese-language romanization"><span style="font-style: normal" lang="yue-Latn">baak3 dou6</span></span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Cantonese" title="Help:IPA/Cantonese">IPA</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="IPA" lang="yue-Latn-fonipa" style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Cantonese" title="Help:IPA/Cantonese">[pak̚˧&#160;tɔw˨]</a></span></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="color: #202122;background-color: #dcffc9;"><a href="/wiki/Southern_Min" title="Southern Min">Southern Min</a></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Hokkien" title="Hokkien">Hokkien</a> <a href="/wiki/Pe%CC%8Dh-%C5%8De-j%C4%AB" title="Pe̍h-ōe-jī">POJ</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><span title="Min Nan Chinese-language romanization"><span style="font-style: normal" lang="nan-Latn">Pah-to͘</span></span></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">
</td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">
</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://ir.baidu.com/">ir<wbr />.baidu<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Baidu, Inc.</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/aɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;tide&#39;">aɪ</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span><span title="/uː/: &#39;oo&#39; in &#39;goose&#39;">uː</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">BY</span>-doo</i></a>; <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>&#58; <span lang="zh">百度</span>; <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">pinyin</a>&#58; <i><span lang="zh-Latn">Bǎidù</span></i>; <abbr title="Literal translation"><small>lit.</small></abbr> &#39;hundred times&#39;) is a Chinese multinational <a href="/wiki/Technology_company" title="Technology company">technology company</a> specializing in <a href="/wiki/Internet_services" class="mw-redirect" title="Internet services">Internet services</a> and <a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>. It holds a dominant position in China's <a href="/wiki/Search_engine" title="Search engine">search engine</a> market (via Baidu Search), and provides a wide variety of other internet services such as Baidu App (Baidu's flagship app for search and newsfeed), <a href="/wiki/Baidu_Baike" title="Baidu Baike">Baidu Baike</a> (an online user created <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia" title="Wikipedia">Wikipedia</a>-like <a href="/wiki/Encyclopedia" title="Encyclopedia">encyclopedia</a>), <a href="/wiki/IQIYI" title="IQIYI">iQIYI</a> (a video streaming service), and <a href="/wiki/Baidu_Tieba" title="Baidu Tieba">Baidu Tieba</a> (a keyword-based discussion forum similar to <a href="/wiki/Reddit" title="Reddit">Reddit</a>).
</p><p>Besides its core internet search business, Baidu has also diversified into other areas. Including <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_driving" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous driving">autonomous driving</a> (Baidu Apollo)<sup id="cite&#95;ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>, smart <a href="/wiki/Consumer_electronics" title="Consumer electronics">consumer electronics</a> (Xiaodu).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and a full-service <a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">AI</a> stack, including software, chips, <a href="/wiki/Cloud_computing" title="Cloud computing">cloud infrastructure</a>, <a href="/wiki/Foundation_models" class="mw-redirect" title="Foundation models">foundation models</a>, and applications.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/Variable_interest_entity" title="Variable interest entity">variable interest entity</a> for Baidu to enable investment of foreign capital is incorporated in the <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">Cayman Islands</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ir.baidu.com&#95;2-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ir.baidu.com-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Baidu was incorporated in January 2000 by <a href="/wiki/Robin_Li" title="Robin Li">Robin Li</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eric_Xu" title="Eric Xu">Eric Xu</a>. Baidu has origins in RankDex, an earlier search engine developed by Robin Li in 1996, before he founded Baidu in 2000.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-rankdex&#95;6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rankdex-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The company is headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Haidian_District" class="mw-redirect" title="Haidian District">Haidian District</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:1&#95;7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2007, Baidu became the first Chinese company to be included in the <a href="/wiki/NASDAQ-100" class="mw-redirect" title="NASDAQ-100">NASDAQ-100</a> index.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As of May 2018, Baidu's <a href="/wiki/Market_capitalization" title="Market capitalization">market cap</a> rose to US$99&#160;billion.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In October 2018, Baidu became the first Chinese firm to join the United States–based computer ethics consortium <a href="/wiki/Partnership_on_AI" title="Partnership on AI">Partnership on AI</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The Chinese government views Baidu as one of its <a href="/wiki/National_champions" title="National champions">national champion</a> corporations.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:Curtis&amp;Klaus&#95;13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:Curtis&amp;Klaus-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Pages: 156–157">&#58;&#8202;156–157&#8202;</span></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baidu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Early_development">Early development</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baidu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early development"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Baidu_headquarters_at_Shangdi_(20220509112439).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Baidu_headquarters_at_Shangdi_%2820220509112439%29.jpg/250px-Baidu_headquarters_at_Shangdi_%2820220509112439%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Baidu_headquarters_at_Shangdi_%2820220509112439%29.jpg/500px-Baidu_headquarters_at_Shangdi_%2820220509112439%29.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="2688" /></a><figcaption>Baidu headquarters building completed in 2009</figcaption></figure>
<p>In 1994, <a href="/wiki/Robin_Li" title="Robin Li">Robin Li</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">Pinyin</a>: Li Yanhong, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>&#58; <span lang="zh">李彦宏</span>) joined IDD Information Services, a <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a> division of <a href="/wiki/Dow_Jones_and_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Dow Jones and Company">Dow Jones and Company</a>, where he helped develop software for the online edition of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He also worked on developing better algorithms for search engines and remained at IDD Information Services from May 1994 to June 1997.
</p><p>In 1996, while at IDD, Li developed the RankDex site-scoring algorithm for search engines results page ranking<sup id="cite&#95;ref-rankdex&#95;6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rankdex-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and received a US patent for the technology.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Launched in 1996,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-rankdex&#95;6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rankdex-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> RankDex was the first search engine that used hyperlinks to measure the quality of websites it was indexing.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Li referred to his search mechanism as "link analysis," which involved ranking the popularity of a web site based on how many other sites had linked to it.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-nytimes&#95;19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It predated the similar <a href="/wiki/PageRank" title="PageRank">PageRank</a> algorithm used by <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> two years later in 1998;<sup id="cite&#95;ref-forbes&#95;20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Google founder <a href="/wiki/Larry_Page" title="Larry Page">Larry Page</a> referenced Li's work as a citation in some of his U.S. patents for PageRank.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-rankdex&#95;6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rankdex-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-forbes&#95;20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Li later used his RankDex technology for the Baidu search engine.
</p><p>Baidu was incorporated on 18 January 2000 by Robin Li and <a href="/wiki/Eric_Xu" title="Eric Xu">Eric Xu</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:1&#95;7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2001, Baidu allowed advertisers to bid for ad space then pay Baidu every time a customer clicked on an ad, predating Google's approach to advertising.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-nytimes&#95;19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2003, Baidu launched a news search engine and picture search engine, adopting a special identification technology capable of identifying and grouping the articles.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="2005:_Public_Listing_on_NASDAQ">2005: Public Listing on NASDAQ</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baidu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 2005: Public Listing on NASDAQ"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Baidu went public on Wall Street through a <a href="/wiki/Variable_interest_entity" title="Variable interest entity">variable interest entity</a> (VIE) based in the <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">Cayman Islands</a> on 5 August 2005.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2007, <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Government of the People&#39;s Republic of China">Chinese government</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese industry">Chinese industry</a> sources stated that Baidu received a license from Beijing, which allows the search engine to become a full-fledged news website. Thus Baidu is able to provide its own reports, besides showing certain results as a search engine. Baidu was the first Chinese search engine to receive such a license.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Baidu started its Japanese language search service, run by Baidu Japan, the company's first regular service outside of China in 2008.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Japanese search engine closed on 16 March 2015.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On 31 July 2012, Baidu announced that it would team up with <a href="/wiki/Sina_Corp" class="mw-redirect" title="Sina Corp">Sina</a> to provide mobile search results.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On 18 November 2012, Baidu announced that it would be partnering with <a href="/wiki/Qualcomm" title="Qualcomm">Qualcomm</a> to offer free cloud storage to <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> users with <a href="/wiki/Snapdragon_(system_on_chip)" class="mw-redirect" title="Snapdragon (system on chip)">Snapdragon</a> processors.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On 2 August 2013, Baidu launched its Personal Assistant app, designed to help CEOs, managers and the white-collar workers manage their business relationships.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On 16 May 2014, Baidu appointed <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Ng" title="Andrew Ng">Dr. Andrew Ng</a> as chief scientist. Dr. Ng will lead Baidu Research in Silicon Valley and Beijing.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On 18 July 2014, the company launched a Brazilian version of the search engine, <i>Baidu Busca</i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On 9 October 2014, Baidu announced acquisition of Brazilian local e-commerce site Peixe Urbano.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="2017:_Launch_of_Autonomous_Driving_Business">2017: Launch of Autonomous Driving Business</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baidu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2017: Launch of Autonomous Driving Business"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In April 2017, Baidu announced the launch of its <a href="/wiki/Apolong" title="Apolong">Apollo project (Apolong)</a>, a self-driving vehicle platform, in a bid to help drive the development of <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_car" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous car">autonomous cars</a> including vehicle platform, hardware platform, open-source software platform and cloud data services.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Baidu plans to launch this project in July 2017, before gradually introducing fully autonomous driving capabilities on highways and open city roads by 2020.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In September 2017, Baidu launched a $1.5billion autonomous driving fund to invest in as many as 100 autonomous driving projects over the ensuing three years.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> At the same time, Apollo open-source software version 1.5 was also launched.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2017, Baidu partnered with <a href="/wiki/Continental_AG" title="Continental AG">Continental</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Bosch_GmbH" class="mw-redirect" title="Robert Bosch GmbH">Bosch</a>, auto industry suppliers, on automated driving and connected cars.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2017, Baidu GBU entered into a partnership with <a href="/wiki/Snap_Inc." title="Snap Inc.">Snap Inc.</a> to act as the company's official ad reseller for Snapchat in <a href="/wiki/Greater_China" title="Greater China">Greater China</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The partnership was extended in 2019.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2017, Baidu rolled out a new portable talking translator that can listen and speak in several different languages. Smaller than a typical smartphone, the 140-gram translation device can also be used as a portable Wi-Fi router and is able to operate on networks in 80 countries. It is still under development. Baidu will also be inserting artificial intelligence (AI) technology into smartphones, through its deep learning platform.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> At the same period, it has also led a joint investment of US$12billion with <a href="/wiki/Alibaba_Group" title="Alibaba Group">Alibaba Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tencent" title="Tencent">Tencent</a>, <a href="/wiki/JD.com" title="JD.com">JD.com</a> and <a href="/wiki/Didi_Chuxing" class="mw-redirect" title="Didi Chuxing">Didi Chuxing</a>, acquiring 35% of <a href="/wiki/China_Unicom" title="China Unicom">China Unicom</a>'s stakes.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2017, according to <i>The Wall Street Journal</i>, Baidu would launch <a href="/wiki/Apolong" title="Apolong">self-driving buses</a> in China in 2018.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the same month, Baidu announced that its first annual Baidu World technology conference (<i>Bring AI to Life</i>) would be held and live-streamed on 16 November 2017, at China World Summit Wing and Kerry Hotel, bringing together Baidu executives, employees, partners, developers, and media to discuss the company's mission and strategy, technology breakthroughs, new product developments, and its open artificial-intelligence (AI) ecosystem.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>China's government designated Baidu as one of its "AI <a href="/wiki/National_champions" title="National champions">champions</a>" in 2018.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:Zhang&#95;48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:Zhang-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 281">&#58;&#8202;281&#8202;</span></sup>
</p><p>In 2018, Baidu divested the "Global DU business" portion of its overseas business, which developed a series of utility apps including ES File Explorer, DU Caller, Mobojoy, Photo Wonder and DU Recorder, etc.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This business now operates independently of Baidu under the name DO Global.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="2021:_Hong_Kong_Secondary_Listing">2021: Hong Kong Secondary Listing</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baidu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2021: Hong Kong Secondary Listing"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In March 2021, Baidu secured a secondary listing on the Hong Kong Stock Exchange, raising $3.1 billion. This marked the largest homecoming for a U.S.-traded Chinese company in Hong Kong since JD.com's listing the previous June. 
</p><p>In August 2021 Baidu revealed a new <a href="/wiki/Self-driving_car" title="Self-driving car">Robocar</a> concept said to be capable of Level 5 autonomous driving.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It also comes with the latest second-generation AI chip that can analyse the internal and external surroundings to provide predictive suggestions to proactively serve the needs of passengers.
</p><p>In June 2022, <a href="/wiki/Jidu_Auto" title="Jidu Auto">Jidu Auto</a>, an intelligent electric vehicle company originally backed by Baidu and Geely unveiled its first concept ROBO-01 in the form of a pre-production vehicle. The ROBO-01 rides on the <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Experience_Architecture_platform" class="mw-redirect" title="Sustainable Experience Architecture platform">Sustainable Experience Architecture</a> (SEA) platform, a modular electric vehicle platform developed by <a href="/wiki/Geely_Holding_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Geely Holding Group">Geely Holding</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2023, Baidu publicly unveiled <a href="/wiki/Ernie_Bot" title="Ernie Bot">Ernie Bot</a>, its <a href="/wiki/Large_language_model" title="Large language model">large language model</a> <a href="/wiki/Chatbot" title="Chatbot">chatbot</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In October 2023, Baidu released a newer version Ernie 4.0 chatbot.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In September 2023, the search engine launched a chatbot based on its <a href="/wiki/Generative_AI" class="mw-redirect" title="Generative AI">generative AI</a> model, GenAI Ernie.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2026, Baidu filed a listing application on the Hong Kong Stock Exchange for their semiconductor unit, Kunlunxin.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Robotaxi">Robotaxi</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baidu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Robotaxi"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Baidu_robotaxi" class="mw-redirect" title="Baidu robotaxi">Baidu robotaxi</a></div>
<p>As of April 2024, Apollo Go, Baidu's autonomous ride-hailing service, had completed six million rides using driverless robotaxis across 11 cities. The service operates a fleet of over 400 driverless vehicles in Wuhan.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2025, Baidu announced its partnership with Uber, allowing it to deploy the Apollo Go outside the U.S and mainland China.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Domain_name_redirection_attack">Domain name redirection attack</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baidu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Domain name redirection attack"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>On 12 January 2010, Baidu.com's DNS records in the United States were altered such that browsers to baidu.com were redirected to a website purporting to be the <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Cyber_Army" title="Iranian Cyber Army">Iranian Cyber Army</a>, thought to be behind the attack on <a href="/wiki/Twitter" class="mw-redirect" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> during the <a href="/wiki/2009_Iranian_election_protests" class="mw-redirect" title="2009 Iranian election protests">2009 Iranian election protests</a>, making the proper site unusable for four hours.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Internet users were met with a page saying "This site has been attacked by Iranian Cyber Army".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Chinese hackers responded by attacking Iranian websites and leaving messages.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-guard&#95;62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guard-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
Baidu later launched legal action against <a href="/wiki/Register.com" title="Register.com">Register.com</a> for gross negligence after it was revealed that Register.com's technical support staff changed the email address for Baidu.com on the request of an unnamed individual, despite failing security verification procedures. Once the address had been changed, the individual was able to use the forgotten password feature to have Baidu's domain passwords sent directly to them, allowing them to accomplish the <a href="/wiki/Domain_hijacking" title="Domain hijacking">domain hijacking</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The lawsuit was settled out of court under undisclosed terms after Register.com issued an apology.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Baidu_workers_arrested">Baidu workers arrested</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baidu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Baidu workers arrested"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>On 6 August 2012, the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> reported that three employees of Baidu were arrested on suspicion that they accepted bribes. The bribes were allegedly paid for deleting posts from the forum service. Four people were fired in connection with these arrests.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="91_Wireless_acquisition">91 Wireless acquisition</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baidu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 91 Wireless acquisition"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>On 16 July 2013, Baidu announced its intention to purchase <a href="/wiki/91_Wireless" title="91 Wireless">91 Wireless</a> from <a href="/wiki/NetDragon" class="mw-redirect" title="NetDragon">NetDragon</a>. 91 Wireless is best known for its app store, but it has been reported that the app store faces privacy and other legal issues.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On 14 August 2013, Baidu announced that its wholly owned subsidiary Baidu (Hong Kong) Limited has signed a definitive merger agreement to acquire 91 Wireless Web-soft Limited from <a href="/wiki/NetDragon" class="mw-redirect" title="NetDragon">NetDragon</a> Web-soft Inc.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> for $1.85&#160;billion in what was reported to be the biggest deal ever in China's IT sector.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="2024:_Artificial_Intelligence_Launch">2024: Artificial Intelligence Launch</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baidu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2024: Artificial Intelligence Launch"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>On 16 March 2025, Baidu released two new artificial intelligence models: ERNIE 4.5, a foundation model, and ERNIE X1, a reasoning model. Baidu claimed that ERNIE X1 performs comparably to <a href="/wiki/DeepSeek" title="DeepSeek">DeepSeek</a>'s R1 model at half the price.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Name">Name</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baidu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Name"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The name <i>Baidu</i> (<span lang="zh">百度</span>) literally means "a hundred times", or alternatively, "countless times". It is a quote from the last line of <a href="/wiki/Xin_Qiji" title="Xin Qiji">Xin Qiji</a>'s (<span lang="zh">辛弃疾</span>) classical poem "Green Jade Table in The Lantern Festival" (<span lang="zh">青玉案·元夕</span>) saying: "Having searched hundreds of times in the crowd, suddenly turning back, she is there in the dimmest candlelight." (<span lang="zh-Hans">众里寻他千<b>百度</b>, 蓦然回首, 那人却在灯火阑珊处。</span>)<sup id="cite&#95;ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Travel">Travel</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baidu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Travel"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Qunar" title="Qunar">Qunar</a> (Qunar Cayman Islands Limited), is a travel-booking service controlled by Baidu. As of 2013, Qunar had 31.4&#160;million active users and raised $167 Million at its <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">initial public offering</a> that year.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is listed at NASDAQ.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Advertisements">Advertisements</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baidu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Advertisements"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Baidu's primary advertising product is called Baidu Tuiguang and is similar to <a href="/wiki/Google_Ads" title="Google Ads">Google Ads</a> and <a href="/wiki/AdSense" class="mw-redirect" title="AdSense">AdSense</a>. It is a <a href="/wiki/Pay_per_click" class="mw-redirect" title="Pay per click">pay per click</a> advertising platform that allows advertisers to have their ads shown in Baidu search results pages and on other websites that are part of Baidu Union. However, Baidu's search results are also based on payments by advertisers. This has prompted criticism and skepticism among Chinese users, with <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Daily" title="People&#39;s Daily">People's Daily</a> commenting in 2018 on issues regarding reliability of Baidu results. Often as many as the first two pages of search results tend to be paid advertisers.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Baidu sells its advertising products via a network of resellers.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Baidu's web administrative tools are all in Chinese, making it difficult for non-Chinese speakers to use. In 2012, a third-party company developed a tool with an interface in English for advertising on Baidu.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Advertisers on Baidu must have a registered business address either in China or in specified East Asian countries.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Competition">Competition</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baidu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Competition"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Baidu<sup id="cite&#95;ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> competes with <a href="/wiki/Sogou" title="Sogou">Sogou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Google_Search" title="Google Search">Google Search</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qihoo" class="mw-redirect" title="Qihoo">360</a> Search (www.so.com), <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Yahoo! China">Yahoo! China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Bing_(search_engine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bing (search engine)">Bing</a> and <a href="/wiki/MSN_Messenger" title="MSN Messenger">MSN Messenger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sina.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Sina.com">Sina</a>, <a href="/wiki/NetEase" title="NetEase">NetEase</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Youdao" title="Youdao">Youdao</a> and PaiPai, <a href="/wiki/Alibaba_Group" title="Alibaba Group">Alibaba</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Taobao" title="Taobao">Taobao</a>, <a href="/wiki/TOM_Online" title="TOM Online">TOM Online</a>, <a href="/wiki/DuckDuckGo" title="DuckDuckGo">DuckDuckGo</a>, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=EachNet&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="EachNet (page does not exist)">EachNet</a>.
</p><p>Baidu is the most used search engine in China, controlling 76.05 percent of China's market share. The <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_number_of_Internet_users" title="List of countries by number of Internet users">number of Internet users</a> in China had reached 705 million by the end of 2015, according to a report by the internetlivestats.com.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In an August 2010 <i>Wall Street Journal</i> article,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Baidu played down its benefit from <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a>'s having moved its China search service to <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, but Baidu's share of revenue in China's search-advertising market grew six percentage points in the second quarter to 70%, according to Beijing-based research firm Analysys International.
</p><p>It is also evident that Baidu is attempting to enter the Internet social network market. As of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Baidu&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, it is discussing the possibility of working with Facebook, which would lead to a Chinese version of the international social network, managed by Baidu.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This plan, if executed, would face off Baidu with competition from the three popular Chinese social networks <a href="/wiki/Qzone" title="Qzone">Qzone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Renren" title="Renren">Renren</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Kaixin001" title="Kaixin001">Kaixin001</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> as well as induce rivalry with instant-messaging giant, <a href="/wiki/Tencent_QQ" title="Tencent QQ">Tencent QQ</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On 22 February 2012, <a href="/wiki/Hudong" class="mw-redirect" title="Hudong">Hudong</a> submitted a complaint to the <a href="/wiki/State_Administration_for_Industry_and_Commerce" title="State Administration for Industry and Commerce">State Administration for Industry and Commerce</a> asking for a review of the behavior of Baidu, accusing it of being monopolistic.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>By August 2014, Baidu's search market share in China dropped to 56.3%, where Qihoo 360, its closest competitor who has rebranded its search engine as so.com, has increased its market share to 29.0%, according to report from CNZZ.com.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2015, Baidu was alleged to have used anticompetitive tactics in Brazil against the Brazilian online security firm PSafe and <a href="/wiki/Qihoo_360" title="Qihoo 360">Qihoo 360</a> (the largest investor of PSafe).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In an ongoing competition in AI natural language processing called <a href="/wiki/General_Language_Understanding_Evaluation" class="mw-redirect" title="General Language Understanding Evaluation">General Language Understanding Evaluation</a>, otherwise known as GLUE, Baidu took a lead over Microsoft and Google in December 2019.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-BaiduMITTechnologyReview&#95;91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BaiduMITTechnologyReview-91"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Research_and_patents">Research and patents</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baidu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Research and patents"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Baidu has started to invest in <a href="/wiki/Deep_learning" title="Deep learning">deep learning</a> research and is integrating new deep learning technology into some of its apps and products, including Phoenix Nest. Phoenix Nest is Baidu's ad-bidding platform.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2012 Baidu JDC long live applied for a patent for its "DNA copyright recognition" technology. This technology automatically scans files that are uploaded by Internet users, and recognizes and filters out content that may violate copyright law. This allows Baidu to offer an infringement-free platform.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2022, Baidu announced they gained permits from China to provide the first driverless taxis. The company aim to provide driverless ride-hailing services to the public and have 10 autonomous cars set to begin offering rides to passengers within a 23-square-mile area in suburban begin beginning 28 April 2022.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2022, Baidu unveiled the <a href="/wiki/Apollo_RT6" class="mw-redirect" title="Apollo RT6">Apollo RT6</a>, a driverless vehicle that is planned to join Baidu's driverless fleet in 2023.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Finances">Finances</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baidu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Finances"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The key trends for Baidu are (as of the financial year ending December 31)
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center">
<tbody><tr>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Censorship">Censorship</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baidu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Censorship"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>According to the <i><a href="/wiki/China_Digital_Times" title="China Digital Times">China Digital Times</a></i>, Baidu has a long history of being the most active and restrictive online censor in the search arena. Documents leaked in April 2009 from an employee in Baidu's internal monitoring and censorship department show a long list of blocked websites and censored topics on Baidu search.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>100<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2011, activists sued Baidu in the United States for violating the U.S. Constitution by the censorship it conducts in accord with the demand of the Chinese government.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>101<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A U.S. judge has ruled<sup id="cite&#95;ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>102<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> that the Chinese search engine Baidu has the right to block works from its query results under <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_speech" title="Freedom of speech">freedom of speech</a> rights, dismissing a lawsuit that sought to punish the company.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>103<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>104<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2017, Baidu began coordinating with the Chinese <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Public_Security_(China)" title="Ministry of Public Security (China)">Ministry of Public Security</a> as well as 372 Internet police departments to detect information related to "anti-government rumors" and then flooding "Baidu-linked web sites, news sites and devices with alerts dispelling misinformation."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:9&#95;105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:9-105"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>105<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This was done using <a href="/wiki/Natural_language_processing" title="Natural language processing">natural language processing</a>, big data and artificial intelligence.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:9&#95;105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:9-105"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>105<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>As part of the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>, Chinese regulators instructed Baidu, along with other Internet companies, to "conduct special supervision" on news and information related to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19" title="COVID-19">disease</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>106<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2022, <a href="/wiki/Sustainalytics" title="Sustainalytics">Sustainalytics</a> downgraded Baidu to "non-compliant" with the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Global_Compact" title="United Nations Global Compact">United Nations Global Compact</a> principles due to complicity with censorship.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>107<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Controversies">Controversies</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baidu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Controversies"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Criticisms_of_Baidu" title="Criticisms of Baidu">Criticisms of Baidu</a></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Death_of_Wei_Zexi">Death of Wei Zexi</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baidu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Death of Wei Zexi"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Wei_Zexi" title="Death of Wei Zexi">Death of Wei Zexi</a></div>
<p>In 2016, Baidu's P4P search results reportedly contributed to the death of a student who tried an experimental cancer therapy he found online. The 21-year-old college student was named Wèi Zéxī (魏则西), who studied in <a href="/wiki/Xidian_University" title="Xidian University">Xidian University</a>. Wei was diagnosed with <a href="/wiki/Synovial_sarcoma" title="Synovial sarcoma">synovial sarcoma</a>, a rare form of cancer. He found the Second Hospital of the Beijing Armed Police Corps (武警北京市总队第二医院) through the search engine Baidu, on which the hospital had been promoting itself.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:8&#95;108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-108"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>108<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The treatment proved unsuccessful and Wèi died in April 2016.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:8&#95;108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-108"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>108<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>After Wei's family spent around 200,000 yuan (around US$31,150) for treatment in the hospital, Wei Zexi died on 12 April 2016. The incident triggered massive online discussions after Wei's death.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>109<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On 2 May 2016, <a href="/wiki/Cyberspace_Administration_of_China" title="Cyberspace Administration of China">Cyberspace Administration of China</a> (CAC), the top watchdog for China's Internet space, dispatched a team of investigators to Baidu.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>110<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The case is still ongoing. One report claimed medical advertising makes up for 30% of Baidu's ad revenue, much of which comes from for-profit hospitals that belong to the "Putian Network", a collection of hospitals across the country founded by medical entrepreneurs associated with the <a href="/wiki/Putian" title="Putian">Putian</a> region of Fujian province.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>111<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The investigation led Chinese regulators to impose several restrictions on Baidu, including adding disclaimers to promotional content and establishing channels for complaints about Baidu services.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>112<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In addition, Baidu's search function now largely directs users to contents published on platforms under Baidu's control, Chinese media scholar Fang Kecheng to proclaim that "Search engine Baidu is dead".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Commercialization_of_Tieba">Commercialization of Tieba</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baidu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Commercialization of Tieba"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Baidu sold the hemophilia online community, one of the communities of <a href="/wiki/Baidu_Tieba" title="Baidu Tieba">Tieba</a>, to unqualified hospitals. In January 2016, Baidu announced that it will stop selling all of its illness-related Tieba.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>114<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On 12 January, Baidu officially announced to the public that all Baidu Tieba for all types of diseases will completely stop commercial cooperation and will only be open to authoritative public welfare organizations. In response to Baidu's decision, Lin Jinlong, president of the Hunan Medical and Health Industry Association, said that private hospitals have entered a period of industry transformation and upgrading, and are neither dependent on posting bar ads nor counting on competitive rankings anymore, so Baidu's decision will not have a negative impact on the industry.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="DO_Global_subsidiary_ad-fraud_in_downloaded_apps">DO Global subsidiary ad-fraud in downloaded apps</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baidu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: DO Global subsidiary ad-fraud in downloaded apps"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>On 20 April 2019, it was reported that several applications for <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> devices developed by the subsidiary company, DO Global (formerly DU Group), were surreptitiously running revenue enhancing background programs on user devices since at least 2016.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Silver&#95;116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Silver-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These programs, part of six known applications developed by the company, and downloaded hundreds of millions times, were <a href="/wiki/Confused_deputy_problem" title="Confused deputy problem">clicking on internet ads</a> – even when the devices were idle, and unbeknownst to <a href="/wiki/End_users" class="mw-redirect" title="End users">end users</a>, to increase <a href="/wiki/Pay-per-click" title="Pay-per-click">revenue generated by "clicks"</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Silver&#95;116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Silver-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Just one of the apps, all of which were available on <a href="/wiki/Google_Play_Store" class="mw-redirect" title="Google Play Store">Google Play Store</a>, had been downloaded 50 million times alone and carried a user rating of 4.5 stars by tens of thousands.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Silver&#95;116-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Silver-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Google banned DO Global and more than 100 of its apps from the <a href="/wiki/Google_Play_Store" class="mw-redirect" title="Google Play Store">Google Play Store</a> on 26 April 2019.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:0&#95;117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-117"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>117<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>118<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> DO Global was also banned from <a href="/wiki/AdMob" title="AdMob">Google's AdMob</a> Network.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:0&#95;117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-117"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>117<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Apps from another developer, ES Global, including the <a href="/wiki/ES_File_Explorer" title="ES File Explorer">ES File Explorer</a>, that were owned by DO Global were banned from the Play Store and the account was suspended.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:2&#95;119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-119"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-:3&#95;120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-120"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>120<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-:4&#95;121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-121"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>122<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-:5&#95;123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-123"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>123<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-:6&#95;124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-124"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>124<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-:7&#95;125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-125"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>125<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Block_in_India">Block in India</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baidu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Block in India"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In August 2020, following the <a href="/wiki/2020_China%E2%80%93India_skirmishes" class="mw-redirect" title="2020 China–India skirmishes">2020 China–India skirmishes</a>, Baidu was one of several Chinese websites that were banned or blocked in India for national security reasons.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="2024_head_of_communications_controversy">2024 head of communications controversy</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baidu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: 2024 head of communications controversy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In May 2024, Baidu's former vice president and head of communications <a href="/w/index.php?title=Qu_Jing&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Qu Jing (page does not exist)">Qu Jing</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E7%92%A9%E9%9D%9C" class="extiw" title="zh:璩靜">zh</a>&#93;</span> (<a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>&#58; <span lang="zh">璩静</span>) sparked major backlashes across the Chinese social media for endorsing toxic workplace culture, where, according to a <a href="/wiki/TikTok" title="TikTok">Douyin</a> video, she has asked a coworker to be on a 50-day business trip during the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>127<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The report has aroused further discussions amongst Chinese <a href="/wiki/Netizen" title="Netizen">netizens</a> regarding Baidu's corporate governance and internal culture. Qu openly apologized after the incident and has allegedly lost her job. Baidu’s stock price fell 2.17% in Hong Kong following the incident.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>128<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>129<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
